- Adicionalmente te pregunto si hay ficha técnica de los actuadores.

 

- De los motores no se requiere certificado. Se solicita el porcentaje que representan los motores en el valor total facturado por proyecto.

内容: Hi Felipe and Yaogang

 

I have reviewed the new grounding reaction that shared by chulong, the reaction have reduced a lot due to the reduction of wind speed and the modification of wind tunnel model.

 

So we don’t need to divide the project site into different area, I have merged Area A and B, and the pile depth results have shown below.

 



 

But there are some issues need to be noted,

 

1.     The recommended foundation type of this project is pre-drilling, because there are lots of piles have been refused in the pot test. And if pre-drilling also be refused, Micropile need to be used as an alternative choice. This issue need to be mentioned to client.

2.     As we discussed before, there are some issues in H19 data, so H19 is disregarded in the depth results above.

 

If you have any other questions, pls let me know.

It should be noted that locations H1, H3, H9, and the overlooked H19 in Area B all feature piles at a depth of 1.5m. Based on the results, the 1.5m piles tested in Area B generally reached their maximum displacement limit at 20kN.

 

Other test results indicate that all 2m piles tested at the project site have excellent data, reaching their maximum displacement limit around 30-40kN.

 

Based on the above analysis, I continue to recommend to the client that 3-4 additional tests be conducted in Area B to replace locations H1, H3, H9, and H19.

 

It is expected that these locations in Area B will yield better test results. This will allow us to further reduce the pile length in Area B, even use the pile length of area A instead of the pile length of area B.

 

Finally, thanks to Luiz for the good explanation. And thanks to the LAC presales and sales teams for your hard work on this project. Hope all is well with you all.

Hi Luiz and Zhitao,

 

After reviewing your comments, it is important to mention that we cannot design post depths greater than 3m, as this would exceed the limits of the pile-driving machines available in Chile.

 

After discussing with the sales team, please disregard the H19 result. In case concrete is required in other areas, kindly consider using micropiles, since if predrilling is necessary, the use of a concrete collar would not make sense.

 

Additionally, please update the foundation solution based on the latest structural calculation shared by Chulong, considering the VG2P SLWD.

Hi LAC Team

 

As discussed with Luiz, we zoned the project site and optimized the pile depth to make the proposal more competitive.

 

It's important to note that the tensile data at H19 was very poor, but the Lateral data was very good. This could be because the Lateral test applied excessive force, causing excessive deformation of the soil around the pile, which resulted in poor tensile test data. The data at the adjacent W19 point was much better.

 

If possible, we could communicate this situation with the client. If the situation is as expected, we could conduct additional tensile tests at this point, or use only the W19 data at this point and ignore the H19 data (the two tests were conducted at the same coordinates). This data could cause our calculations to be very complex(Personally, I don't want to use this data, but I can't ignore it. This data makes the pile length will be very long, as will be shown below). If the above situation is confirmed, we can use the calculation results of Area B instead of Area C. 

 

Aera A accounts for approximately 80%, Area B accounts for approximately 15%, and Area C accounts for approximately 5%.

各位同事：


前段时间，天合跟踪市场团队向海外同事分享了新版销售工具格式。此次更新旨在强化事业部的视觉识别体系与沟通一致性，同时保持与天合光能集团整体品牌框架的统一。

为确保全球范围内品牌形象及沟通标准的一致，现将此信息同步至中国团队。

近期，总部品牌部（Branding）也向全体员工分发了新版天合光能公司模板和相关资料。
部分同事在日常使用中，对“在不同场景下应使用哪一版本”存在疑问。
为此，我们在此明确相关官方指引如下。


官方使用指引


1. 邮件签名（Email Signatures）


*	天合跟踪（TrinaTracker）与天合光能（Trinasolar）两种签名格式均为官方认可版本。
*	建议优先使用天合光能签名作为标准格式，以维护全球统一的企业形象，强化天合光能作为一体化全球品牌的定位。
*	当邮件内容专门涉及天合跟踪业务时，可继续使用天合跟踪签名。

🔗 链接 1：https://trinabox.trinasolar.com/l/UJYcJq

🔗 链接 2：https://trinabox.trinasolar.com/l/nuNlnb

 


2. PowerPoint 模板（Presentation Templates）


*	当内容仅与天合跟踪相关时，请使用天合跟踪PPT模板。

——🔗 链接 1：https://trinabox.trinasolar.com/l/u1FgjB

*	当演示内容涉及其他业务单元或代表整个天合光能集团时，请使用天合光能企业模板。

——🔗 链接 2：https://trinabox.trinasolar.com/l/I00t21

 

此区分有助于保持天合跟踪事业部的独立识别性，同时确保集团品牌形象的统一与协调。

 


3. 虚拟会议背景（Virtual Backgrounds）


天合跟踪与天合光能两种虚拟背景均为官方认可，具体使用场景如下：

*	内部会议、外部客户会议或事业部专属会议：使用天合跟踪背景。

——🔗 链接 1：https://trinabox.trinasolar.com/l/60jBWh

*	集团级或跨业务线会议：建议使用天合光能背景，以保持全球统一的品牌形象。

——🔗 链接 2：https://trinabox.trinasolar.com/l/31Lbee


总结与要求：


本次指引旨在进一步统一天合跟踪事业部的品牌使用标准，
确保事业部在持续强化自身独特品牌形象的同时，始终与天合光能全球品牌保持一致。

请各位同事在日常沟通与对外展示中，严格遵循以上规范，
共同维护专业、统一、具全球影响力的品牌形象。

感谢大家的配合与支持！

天合跟踪市场团队
TrinaTracker Marketing Team

________________________________

Dear colleagues of the TrinaTracker Division,

Based on branding development needs and feedback from business units, the TrinaTracker Marketing Team has recently upgraded the visual guidelines for the Tracker Business Unit. A few weeks ago, we conducted a pilot test in the Madrid office, sharing the updated Sales Tools format with the local team and collecting feedback through real-world usage to finalize improvements. With the Madrid pilot successfully completed, this communication serves as the official notice to all employees within the Tracker Business Unit, formally initiating the division-wide adoption of the updated materials. The update aims to strengthen the business unit’s visual identity system, enhance the consistency and coherence of communication materials, and ensure alignment with the broader branding framework of Trinasolar Group.

Subsequently, the HQ Branding Team distributed the new Trinasolar corporate templates and relevant materials to all employees. As corporate-level and business-unit-level templates differ in application scenarios, some colleagues have expressed uncertainty regarding which versions should be used in various contexts. To ensure standardized and consistent communication across the organization, the following official guidelines are provided.

 

2. Official Usage Guidelines

1) Email Signatures

Both TrinaTracker and Trinasolar email signatures are officially approved.

*	The Trinasolar signature is recommended as the default option, supporting a unified corporate image and reinforcing Trinasolar as an integrated global brand: https://trinabox.trinasolar.com/l/T55qJZ <https://trinabox.trinasolar.com/l/T55qJZ> 
*	For communications specifically related to the Tracker Business Unit, the TrinaTracker signature remains acceptable:  New signature.docx <https://trinasolarus.sharepoint.com/:w:/s/TrinaTracker_marketing/IQA0g88wPn_0SpgU23JW_Bu7AX4sHz5DWKbONSRatbANbrE?e=v8M5r3> 

 

2) Presentation Templates

*	For content exclusive to the Tracker Business Unit: use the TrinaTracker templates:  TEMPLATE_Tracker (1) v2.pptx <https://trinasolarus.sharepoint.com/:p:/s/TrinaTracker_marketing/IQDy3oTU450OS6MvO7oZzWgUAexVIb7VYsmtfJEh60V-tV8?e=z9rCaR> 
*	For content involving other business units or representing the Trinasolar Group as a whole: use the Trinasolar corporate templates: https://trinabox.trinasolar.com/l/c1crKj <https://trinabox.trinasolar.com/l/c1crKj> 

 

3) Virtual Backgrounds

Both TrinaTracker and Trinasolar virtual backgrounds are approved. Use should be based on the meeting context:

*	For internal/external meetings focused on the Tracker Business Unit: use the TrinaTracker background:  Virtual Background TrinaTracker <https://trinasolarus.sharepoint.com/:f:/s/TrinaTracker_marketing/IgB1_HvOXZssSq5uOQWFnX-YAaIsRHOBjUYHuapXyencnmI?e=n2nKgL> 
*	For corporate-level or multi-business-line meetings: use the Trinasolar background: https://trinabox.trinasolar.com/l/RJnu3l <https://trinabox.trinasolar.com/l/RJnu3l> 

 

3. Summary

These guidelines aim to standardize communication and branding practices across the Tracker Business Unit, ensuring that while the unit strengthens its unique identity, it remains aligned with the global Trinasolar brand.

Please follow these guidelines in daily communication and external presentations to maintain a professional, consistent, and globally aligned brand image.

Thank you for your cooperation and support.

 

TrinaTracker Marketing Team

邮件 18:
发件人: TSL_Information Security（信息安全公告）
主题: 关于OpenClaw智能体的风险提示--Information Security Risk Advisory on the OpenClaw Agent
时间: 2026-03-10 19:14:29.340000+00:00
内容: 

>>Please scroll down for English version

各位同事，大家好!

近期，信息安全运营中心监测发现OpenClaw（曾用名Clawdbot、Moltbot，俗称“龙虾”）存在较高安全风险，极易引发网络攻击、信息泄露等安全问题。据悉，已有企业因员工内网私搭OpenClaw智能体，导致服务器被黑客远程控制，造成业务中断。同时，工信部发布了《关于防范OpenClaw开源AI智能体安全风险的预警提示》，目前OpenClaw存在如下风险：

OpenClaw是一款开源AI智能体，其通过整合多渠道通信能力与大语言模型，构建具备持久记忆、主动执行能力的定制化AI助手，可在本地私有化部署。由于OpenClaw在部署时“信任边界模糊”，且具备自身持续运行、自主决策、调用系统和外部资源等特性，在缺乏有效权限控制、审计机制和安全加固的情况下，可能因指令诱导、配置缺陷或被恶意接管，执行越权操作，造成信息泄露、系统受控等一系列安全风险。

为保障公司信息安全，规范公司工作环境中的智能体使用，现发布如下风险提示：

1、禁止员工自行在公司电脑、服务器上安装、运行OpenClaw及相关衍生版本；

2、信息安全部将持续监测并阻断OpenClaw相关智能体在员工办公电脑的运行。

3、如工作中有OpenClaw等智能体使用需求，请通过数字化需求管理流程申请，数字化团队将安排专业团队对接支持。

信息安全部将持续关注行业主管部门安全公告和加固建议，防范潜在网络安全风险，保障AI时代先进生产力工具在公司安全有序使用。

 

Dear Colleagues,

 

Recently, the Information Security Operations Center detected that OpenClaw (formerly known as Clawdbot and Moltbot) poses significant security risks and is highly susceptible to triggering cyberattacks and data breaches. Several reports indicate that multiple enterprises have experienced business disruptions after employees privately deployed OpenClaw agents on internal networks, resulting in servers being remotely compromised by hackers. Meanwhile, government authorities have issued an “Alert on Preventing Security Risks of OpenClaw Open-Source AI Agents.” The specific risks associated with OpenClaw are as follows:

 

OpenClaw is an open-source AI agent that integrates multi-channel communication capabilities with large language models to create customizable AI assistants featuring persistent memory and proactive execution, capable of being deployed locally and privately. Due to blurred trust boundaries during deployment—combined with its inherent characteristics such as continuous operation, autonomous decision‑making, and the ability to invoke system commands and external resources—it may execute unauthorized operations if effective permission controls, audit mechanisms, and security hardening are lacking. This may occur due to prompt injection, configuration flaws, or malicious takeover, leading to data leaks, system compromise, and other severe security risks.

 

To safeguard the company's information security and regulate the use of AI agents in the workplace, we hereby issue the following advisory:

 

1.	Employees are strictly prohibited from installing or running OpenClaw or its derivative versions on company computers or servers without authorization.
2.	The Information Security Department will continue monitoring and blocking the execution of OpenClaw‑related agents on employee office devices.
3.	If there is a business need to use OpenClaw or similar AI agents, please submit a request through the Digital Demand Management Process. TPD will arrange the necessary professional support accordingly.

 

The Information Security Department will continue to monitor security bulletins and hardening recommendations from industry regulators, mitigate potential cybersecurity risks, and ensure the safe and orderly use of advanced AI-powered productivity tools within the company.

For the Chinu 1–5 and Galeras projects, the BOM specifies FA21 sensors, so they were most likely shipped accordingly.

 

However, in the NCU assembly drawings the sensors are indicated as FA134.

I need confirmation on which one is correct and which one was actually shipped. If the shipped material is not consistent with the BOM and other documents, it may cause issues with customs clearance in Colombia.

Hello @Dankert_Fernando TS/PS <mailto:fernando.dankert@trinasolar.com> ,

 

Reviewed the HDG requirements for the mechanical parts considering the updated atmospheric corrosivity assessment. Based on the latest analysis, we would like to confirm the following:

 

For C4 environments, HDG 55 μm is acceptable for above-ground mechanical parts and remains aligned with the project specifications.

 

For C4-High environments, HDG 65 μm is required to ensure adequate durability.

 

Please note that, after the update of the analyses, the Ponedera project shall be considered as C4-High, therefore requiring HDG 65 μm for mechanical parts (correction from the previous assumption).

 

Below is the updated atmospheric coating table to be used as reference until the final soil and atmospheric corrosion report is issued:

I answer to your questions below:

 

*        As we confirmed the environmental corrosivity is almost C4, could you please tell me the required coating thickness for the mechanical parts using HDG coating under these conditions? Average HDG ≥70μm or ≥85μm? I need to have a double check of the mechanical parts, because not all of them use ZM coating.

All projects can consider 55HDG for above ground coating. Please @Pereira_Polyana TS/CC <mailto:polyana.pereira@trinasolar.com>  and @Teixeira_Luiz TS/CC <mailto:luiz.teixeira@trinasolar.com>  I appreciate your support on this until the soil and atm corrosion report is ready.

 

*        Please list the required coating thickness for the mechanical parts using HDG coating for the six projects one by one? Because they are under different environmental corrosivity conditions.

o   Atmospheric Coatings:

o   Chinu 1:  55HDG & ZM275

o   Chinu 2:  55HDG & ZM275

o   Chinu 3:  55HDG & ZM275

o   Chinu 4:  55HDG & ZM275

o   Chinu 5:  55HDG & ZM275

o   Galeras:  55HDG & ZM275

o   Pivijay: 55HDG & ZM275

o   Luruaco: 55HDG & ZM310.

      

 

*        In the checklist of CHINU 1,2 projects, there were no border trackers. But actually border trackers exist in the final layout. Should I follow the tracker type in the checklist or the detailed types in the layout?

Please consider all as Outer 1C, this is because the customer informed that some changes on the Layout might be needed and in that case the don' want to affect the discretization. The offer and contract were done with this consideration.

Hello Team,

 

In the attempt of trying to reduce the workload for Solenium Projects, the documentation can be delivered as found in column H of the attached file. Having 4 types of documents:

 

General:                     Only one document for the whole of Solenium.

P/Tipología VG1P o VG2P:      Only two types of documents each, one for VG1P Projects and other for the VG2P projects:

                            

 

P/grupo:                    This documents must be prepared for projects that have the same technical considerations due to its location, being:

*        Chinu 1&2

*        Chinu 3, 4 & 5

*        Galeras

*        Pivijay 1, 2 & 3

*        Luruaco

 

P/Projeto                    Only for BOMS. Each 1,35MWp project must have its own BOM:

*        Chinu 1

*        Chinu 2

*        Chinu 3

*        Chinu 4

*        Chinu 5

*        Galeras

*        Pivijay 1

*        Pivijay 2

*        Pivijay 3

*        Luruaco

 

 

With this there is no need to prepare the whole amount of documents for each project.

 

Please let me know if you have any doubt or comment.

Hello @Li_ChuLong TS/SA(李楚龙) <mailto:chulong.li@trinasolar.com> ,

 

For the Chinu 1–5 and Galeras projects, the BOM specifies FA21 sensors, so they were most likely shipped accordingly.

 

However, in the NCU assembly drawings the sensors are indicated as FA134.

 

Therefore, they are different, and apparently it is not possible to install them on the tower.

 

I need confirmation on which one is correct and which one was actually shipped. If the shipped material is not consistent with the BOM and other documents, it may cause issues with customs clearance in Colombia.

Hello @Dankert_Fernando TS/PS <mailto:fernando.dankert@trinasolar.com> ,

 

Reviewed the HDG requirements for the mechanical parts considering the updated atmospheric corrosivity assessment. Based on the latest analysis, we would like to confirm the following:

 

For C4 environments, HDG 55 μm is acceptable for above-ground mechanical parts and remains aligned with the project specifications.

 

For C4-High environments, HDG 65 μm is required to ensure adequate durability.

 

Please note that, after the update of the analyses, the Ponedera project shall be considered as C4-High, therefore requiring HDG 65 μm for mechanical parts (correction from the previous assumption).

I answer to your questions below:

 

*        As we confirmed the environmental corrosivity is almost C4, could you please tell me the required coating thickness for the mechanical parts using HDG coating under these conditions? Average HDG ≥70μm or ≥85μm? I need to have a double check of the mechanical parts, because not all of them use ZM coating.

All projects can consider 55HDG for above ground coating. Please @Pereira_Polyana TS/CC <mailto:polyana.pereira@trinasolar.com>  and @Teixeira_Luiz TS/CC <mailto:luiz.teixeira@trinasolar.com>  I appreciate your support on this until the soil and atm corrosion report is ready.

 

*        Please list the required coating thickness for the mechanical parts using HDG coating for the six projects one by one? Because they are under different environmental corrosivity conditions.

o   Atmospheric Coatings:

o   Chinu 1:  55HDG & ZM275

o   Chinu 2:  55HDG & ZM275

o   Chinu 3:  55HDG & ZM275

o   Chinu 4:  55HDG & ZM275

o   Chinu 5:  55HDG & ZM275

o   Galeras:  55HDG & ZM275

o   Pivijay: 55HDG & ZM275

o   Luruaco: 55HDG & ZM310.

      

 

*        In the checklist of CHINU 1,2 projects, there were no border trackers. But actually border trackers exist in the final layout. Should I follow the tracker type in the checklist or the detailed types in the layout?

Please consider all as Outer 1C, this is because the customer informed that some changes on the Layout might be needed and in that case the don' want to affect the discretization. The offer and contract were done with this consideration.

Hello Team,

 

In the attempt of trying to reduce the workload for Solenium Projects, the documentation can be delivered as found in column H of the attached file. Having 4 types of documents:

 

General:                     Only one document for the whole of Solenium.

P/Tipología VG1P o VG2P:      Only two types of documents each, one for VG1P Projects and other for the VG2P projects:

                            

 

P/grupo:                    This documents must be prepared for projects that have the same technical considerations due to its location, being:

*        Chinu 1&2

*        Chinu 3, 4 & 5

*        Galeras

*        Pivijay 1, 2 & 3

*        Luruaco

 

P/Projeto                    Only for BOMS. Each 1,35MWp project must have its own BOM:

*        Chinu 1

*        Chinu 2

*        Chinu 3

*        Chinu 4

*        Chinu 5

*        Galeras

*        Pivijay 1

*        Pivijay 2

*        Pivijay 3

*        Luruaco

 

 

With this there is no need to prepare the whole amount of documents for each project.

 

Please let me know if you have any doubt or comment.

Hi Chulong,

 

Checking the offers I noticed the 2P42 was designed with 4 motors (9 total post) and the 2P28 with 2 motors (6 total post). This makes the offer using 2P42 increases a lot the total amount of motors (around 30%), even if the total amount of Trackers is 45% less in the 2P42 Layout.

 

Can you please check if it’s possible to design a VG2P 2P42 just using 3 motors? 

 

@Liu_ZhiTao TS/SA(刘志涛) <mailto:zhitao.liu@trinasolar.com>  please update the foundation solution according to these changes.

 

We look forward to your answer.

Hello @Li_ChuLong TS/SA(李楚龙) <mailto:chulong.li@trinasolar.com> ,

 

For the Chinu 1–5 and Galeras projects, the BOM specifies FA21 sensors, so they were most likely shipped accordingly.

 

However, in the NCU assembly drawings the sensors are indicated as FA134.

 

Therefore, they are different, and apparently it is not possible to install them on the tower.

 

I need confirmation on which one is correct and which one was actually shipped. If the shipped material is not consistent with the BOM and other documents, it may cause issues with customs clearance in Colombia.

For the Chinu 1–5 and Galeras projects, the BOM specifies FA21 sensors, so they were most likely shipped accordingly.

 

However, in the NCU assembly drawings the sensors are indicated as FA134.

 

Therefore, they are different, and apparently it is not possible to install them on the tower.

 

I need confirmation on which one is correct and which one was actually shipped. If the shipped material is not consistent with the BOM and other documents, it may cause issues with customs clearance in Colombia.

 

Best regards.
